# CLAIM 2: Permanent Injunction

## Legal Elements
- **A-Likelihood of Success**: Ordinance is preempted/invalid under state law
- **B-Irreparable Harm**: Enforcement threatens criminal liability, business destruction
- **C-Balance of Harms**: Tree Farm loses livelihood vs county loses nothing
- **D-Public Interest**: State policy favors CIM operations / public need for aggregate

---
# PART 1: HIGH INTEREST DOCUMENTS
*These documents contain the strongest evidence. Full text included for attorney review.*

```
Request for Agency Action

Filing Date: March 17, 2022

I, Tamara Prue, being of lawful age, hereby swear and state as follows:
1. I am over 21 years of age.
2. I have personal knowledge of the facts stated herein.
3. I reside in Salt Lake County, Utah.
4. I am the Water Resource Manager for Salt Lake City Corporation (the “City”), and I
have been employed with the City for two years. Prior to my employment with the City, I was an
employee at the State of Utah Division of Water Rights (the “Division”) for 12 years, most recently
2

g

as an Adjudication Team Lead. I have a Horticulture degree from Utah State University.
5. Salt Lake City is the largest retail water provider in the State of Utah and has over 360,000
water customers. The City’s water assets include over 30,000 acres of property in the Wasatch
Mountain range that is designated watershed property. This includes approximately thousands of
acres of land owned by the City in Parleys Canyon. Parleys Canyon also contains the City’s
Parleys Water Treatment Plant, which processes up to 20 percent of the water used by Salt Lake
City water customers. The City maintains two reservoirs for drinking water and flood control in the
Parleys watershed.
6. The water rights in the Parleys Canyon area are administered by the Division, and the
primary guidance for relative share of the water and priority of water rights among the water users
was established by the Decree dated May 2, 1912, that adjudicated the Parleys Creek and waters by
Judge C. W. Morse. See Exhibit A. The Division commenced a modern adjudication for the
Parleys Creek Book (57-14) on October 16, 2017. The adjudication process allows all water users
to assert claims to water rights by filing a water user claim. After all water user claims are filed, the
Division identifies all “unclaimed” water rights to give water users another chance to assert claims
to use water in a drainage area. Through this process, the Division is able to evaluate the validity of
all rights in a particular drainage area.
7. The Division then issues and publishes a Proposed Determination (“PD”), which lists all
known water rights within defined boundaries of the book and identifies them as either “valid” or
“recommended to be forfeited.” The Parleys PD was published on March 1, 2022. See Exhibit B.
The PD also lists all water user claims that were 
... [truncated — full text is 5877 characters]
```

### SLCo006361 — Petition to Intervene
**Element:** B-Irreparable Harm | **Applies to:** Claims 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Enforcement action threatening irreparable harm to plaintiff

> *Key Quote:* Nothing in the statute authorizes
a proponent of a new, large mining operation to circumvent the review and approval process for
a large mining operation by submitting a Small Mine NOI to allow commencement of mining
operations within the footprint of the intended large mining operation before review and
approval of the large mining operation has been completed.

**FULL DOCUMENT TEXT:**
```
Petition to Intervene

Millcreek

H. Michael Keller # 1784
Tanner J. Bean #17128
FABIAN VANCOTT
215 South State Street, Suite 1200
Salt Lake City, Utah 84111
801-574-2622
mkeller@fabianvancott.com
tbean@fabianvancott.com
Counsel for Millcreek

FILED
JANUARY 10 2022
SECRETARY, BOARD OF
OIL, GAS & MINING

BEFORE THE BOARD OF OIL, GAS, AND MINING
DEPARTMENT OF NATURAL RESOURCES
STATE OF UTAH
In the Matter of:
Denial of Notice of Intention to
Commence Small Mining
Operations, Tree Farm LLC, Silver
Mine, S/035/0053, Task ID# 10588,
Salt Lake County, Utah
Request for Agency Action

CITY OF MILLCREEK’S
PETITION TO INTERVENE
Docket No. 2022-002
Cause No. S/035/0053
Filing Date: January 10, 2022

Pursuant to Utah Administrative Code § R641-103-100, the City of Millcreek
(“Millcreek”), a Utah municipal corporation, submits this Petition to Intervene. Millcreek seeks
to intervene for the purposes of (i) supporting the December 7, 2021 denial by the Division of
Oil, Gas and Mining (“Division”) of the Notice of Intention to Commence Small Mining
Operations, Tree Farm LLC, Silver Mine, S/035/0053, Task ID# 10588, Salt Lake County, Utah,
filed by Tree Farm LLC, (ii) and opposing Tree Farm LLC’s Request for Agency Action and any
commencement of mining operations by Tree Farm LLC under a Notice of Intention to
Commence Small Mining Operations. As set forth herein, Millcreek’s legal interests will be
substantially affected by the formal adjudicative proceedings in the above-captioned case, and
the interests of justice and the orderly and prompt conduct of the adjudicative proceedings will

Millcreek’s Petition to Intervene
January 10, 2022
not be materially impaired by allowing Millcreek’s intervention. This Petition is supported by the
Declaration of Mayor Jeff Silvestrini in Support of City of Millcreek’s Petition to Intervene
(“Mayor’s Declaration”), attached as Exhibit A.
STATEMENT OF FACTS
On November 12, 2021, Tree Farm LLC (“Tree Farm”) submitted to the Division both a
Notice of Intention to Commence Small Mining Operations (“Small Mine NOI”) and a Notice of
Intention to Commence Large Mining Operations (“Large Mine NOI”). On December 7, 2021,
the Division denied Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI. It explained that the “contemporaneous
submittal of these NOIs indicates Tree Farm LLC’s long-term intent is to commence operations
for a large mine,” and that in “the interest of administrative efficiency . . . [the Division] will turn
all focus and attention to the expedient review and processing of Tree Farm LLC’s Large Mine
NOI.” On December 10, 2021, Tree Farm filed a Request for Agency Action, seeking a
declaratory ruling from the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining (“Board”) regarding the completeness
of Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI and the sufficiency of its proposed reclamation surety in order
to commence operations under its Small Mine NOI.
Millcreek is a city of more than 63,000 residents located in Salt Lake County. Millcreek
borders the mouth of Parleys Canyon, and
```

```
STATEMENT OF FACTS
On November 12, 2021, Tree Farm LLC (“Tree Farm”) submitted to the Division both a
Notice of Intention to Commence Small Mining Operations (“Small Mine NOI”) and a Notice of
Intention to Commence Large Mining Operations (“Large Mine NOI”). On December 7, 2021,
the Division denied Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI. It explained that the “contemporaneous
submittal of these NOIs indicates Tree Farm LLC’s long-term intent is to commence operations
for a large mine,” and that in “the interest of administrative efficiency . . . [the Division] will turn
all focus and attention to the expedient review and processing of Tree Farm LLC’s Large Mine
NOI.” On December 10, 2021, Tree Farm filed a Request for Agency Action, seeking a
declaratory ruling from the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining (“Board”) regarding the completeness
of Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI and the sufficiency of its proposed reclamation surety in order
to commence operations under its Small Mine NOI.
```

```
Outdoor gear makers gave up their boycott of Utah while gaining nothing, George Pyle writes (The Salt
Lake Tribune, George Pyle)
Salt Lake County Mayor Jenny Wilson, among others, argued that the outdoor gear companies didn’t get the

Salt Lake City and County need to protect their watersheds from fire danger
(The Salt Lake Tribune, Phil Lyman)
Both Salt Lake City Mayor Mendenhall and Salt Lake County Mayor Wilson enthusiastically welcomed OR
back to Salt Lake, touting the city and county’s environmental stewardship.
Salt Lake County receives grant to serve Afghan refugees ( KSL-AM, Samantha Herrera)
Open Society Foundations awarded $150,000 to Salt Lake County Mayor’s Office for New Americans. The grant
will help the office’s Operation Afghan Refugee Support, which provides resources to Afghan refugees in the
county.
'Not the best-case scenario': Early melt offers 'bleak' water outlook in Salt Lake County (KSL, Carter
Williams)
That means state and local governments, such as the Salt Lake County Council, may have to initiate water
conservation goals again this spring and summer to avoid serious issues. Salt Lake County Mayor Jenny Wilson
said county agencies were able to reduce consumption by 13% last year and it's shaping up that the county will
have to cut back again based on the current snowpack and forecast data.
Salt Lake County launches Water Summit to combat drought (KSL, Jed Boal)
Salt Lake County launched a Water Summit Tuesday to focus on critical issues facing all Utahns during the
drought. The four-part series will be held during the County Council work sessions this spring. County Mayor
Jenny Wilson is encouraging everyone to do their part because there’s no one solution to our water shortage.
'We're in a world of hurt': Drought leads to tough restrictions in Weber-Ogden basin (KSL, Amy Joi
O’Donoghue)
While Salt Lake County is not a water provider, it did set a goal of shaving its own water use by 5% last year and
actually achieved a 13% countywide reduction in consumption, with 75% coming from parks and recreation,
according to Lisa Hartman, the associate deputy mayor.
```

```
Meeting Agenda

February 15, 2022

This meeting will be simulcast electronically via Webex Events. Agendas, audio
live-streams and recordings, and meeting minutes can be accessed at slco.legistar.com. The
Council will also broadcast live-streams of its meetings on Facebook Live, which may be
accessed at http://www.facebook.com/slcocouncil/, and through Cisco Webex, which may
be accessed at:
https://slco.webex.com/slco/onstage/g.php?MTID=e978ceeb80941036b21740906fe754ee7
Individuals wishing to comment electronically must access the meeting using the Webex
link above by the beginning of the “Citizen Public Input” portion of the meeting. If an
individual is unable to attend the meeting, they may also email their comments to
councilwebex@slco.org by 10:00 AM the day of the meeting to have those comments
distributed to the Council and read into the record at the appropriate time.
The first time you join via the link may take longer to get through the set-up steps. Please
plan accordingly.
Please include "Resident" ahead of your first name when you join the meeting or you will
not be identified as wanting to give comment.
This website has helpful tips for using Webex for Events:
https://help.webex.com/ld-7srxjs-CiscoWebexEvents/Webex-Events
```

```
Outdoor gear makers gave up their boycott of Utah while gaining nothing, George Pyle writes (The Salt
Lake Tribune, George Pyle)
Salt Lake County Mayor Jenny Wilson, among others, argued that the outdoor gear companies didn’t get the

Salt Lake City and County need to protect their watersheds from fire danger
(The Salt Lake Tribune, Phil Lyman)
Both Salt Lake City Mayor Mendenhall and Salt Lake County Mayor Wilson enthusiastically welcomed OR
back to Salt Lake, touting the city and county’s environmental stewardship.
Salt Lake County receives grant to serve Afghan refugees ( KSL-AM, Samantha Herrera)
Open Society Foundations awarded $150,000 to Salt Lake County Mayor’s Office for New Americans. The grant
will help the office’s Operation Afghan Refugee Support, which provides resources to Afghan refugees in the
county.
'Not the best-case scenario': Early melt offers 'bleak' water outlook in Salt Lake County (KSL, Carter
Williams)
That means state and local governments, such as the Salt Lake County Council, may have to initiate water
conservation goals again this spring and summer to avoid serious issues. Salt Lake County Mayor Jenny Wilson
said county agencies were able to reduce consumption by 13% last year and it's shaping up that the county will
have to cut back again based on the current snowpack and forecast data.
Salt Lake County launches Water Summit to combat drought (KSL, Jed Boal)
Salt Lake County launched a Water Summit Tuesday to focus on critical issues facing all Utahns during the
drought. The four-part series will be held during the County Council work sessions this spring. County Mayor
Jenny Wilson is encouraging everyone to do their part because there’s no one solution to our water shortage.
'We're in a world of hurt': Drought leads to tough restrictions in Weber-Ogden basin (KSL, Amy Joi
O’Donoghue)
While Salt Lake County is not a water provider, it did set a goal of shaving its own water use by 5% last year and
actually achieved a 13% countywide reduction in consumption, with 75% coming from parks and recreation,
according to Lisa Hartman, the associate deputy mayor.
```

### SLCo009088 — Petition to Intervene
**Element:** B-Irreparable Harm | **Applies to:** Claims 2, 4, 5 | **UNDERMINES**

**Legal Significance:** Enforcement action threatening irreparable harm to plaintiff

> *Key Quote:* Nothing in the statute authorizes
a proponent of a new, large mining operation to circumvent the review and approval process for
a large mining operation by submitting a Small Mine NOI to allow commencement of mining
operations within the footprint of the intended large mining operation before review and
approval of the large mining operation has been completed.

```

Millcreek

Cause No. S/035/0053

Pursuant to Utah Administrative Code § R641-103-100, the City of Millcreek
(“Millcreek”), a Utah municipal corporation, submits this Petition to Intervene. Millcreek seeks
to intervene for the purposes of (i) supporting the December 7, 2021 denial by the Division of
Oil, Gas and Mining (“Division”) of the Notice of Intention to Commence Small Mining
Operations, Tree Farm LLC, Silver Mine, S/035/0053, Task ID# 10588, Salt Lake County, Utah,
filed by Tree Farm LLC, (ii) and opposing Tree Farm LLC’s Request for Agency Action and any
commencement of mining operations by Tree Farm LLC under a Notice of Intention to
Commence Small Mining Operations. As set forth herein, Millcreek’s legal interests will be
substantially affected by the formal adjudicative proceedings in the above-captioned case, and
the interests of justice and the orderly and prompt conduct of the adjudicative proceedings will

Millcreek’s Petition to Intervene
January 10, 2022
not be materially impaired by allowing Millcreek’s intervention. This Petition is supported by the
Declaration of Mayor Jeff Silvestrini in Support of City of Millcreek’s Petition to Intervene
(“Mayor’s Declaration”), attached as Exhibit A.
STATEMENT OF FACTS
On November 12, 2021, Tree Farm LLC (“Tree Farm”) submitted to the Division both a
Notice of Intention to Commence Small Mining Operations (“Small Mine NOI”) and a Notice of
Intention to Commence Large Mining Operations (“Large Mine NOI”). On December 7, 2021,
the Division denied Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI. It explained that the “contemporaneous
submittal of these NOIs indicates Tree Farm LLC’s long-term intent is to commence operations
for a large mine,” and that in “the interest of administrative efficiency . . . [the Division] will turn
all focus and attention to the expedient review and processing of Tree Farm LLC’s Large Mine
NOI.” On December 10, 2021, Tree Farm filed a Request for Agency Action, seeking a
declaratory ruling from the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining (“Board”) regarding the completeness
of Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI and the sufficiency of its proposed reclamation surety in order
to commence operations under its Small Mine NOI.
Millcreek is a city of more than 63,000 residents located in Salt Lake County. Millcreek
borders the mouth of Parleys Canyon, and a significant number of Millcreek’s residents live in
an ar
... [truncated — full text is 17900 characters]
```

```
Pursuant to Utah Administrative Code § R641-103-100, Salt Lake City Corporation
(“Salt Lake City”), a Utah municipal corporation, submits this Petition to Intervene. Salt Lake
City seeks to intervene for the purposes of (i) supporting the December 7, 2021 denial by the
Division of Oil, Gas and Mining (“Division”) of the Notice of Intention to Commence Small
Mining Operations, Tree Farm LLC, Silver Mine, S/035/0053, Task ID# 10588, Salt Lake
County, Utah, filed by Tree Farm LLC, (ii) and opposing Tree Farm LLC’s Request for Agency
Action and any commencement of mining operations by Tree Farm LLC under a Notice of
Intention to Commence Small Mining Operations. As set forth herein, Salt Lake City’s legal
interests will be substantially affected by the formal adjudicative proceedings in the above2

Salt Lake City’s Petition to
Intervene January 25, 2022
captioned case, and the interests of justice and the orderly and prompt conduct of the
adjudicative proceedings will not be materially impaired by allowing Salt Lake City’s
intervention. This Petition is supported by the Declaration of Laura Briefer, Director of Salt Lake
City’s Department of Public Utilities in Support of Salt Lake City’s Petition to Intervene
(“Briefer Declaration”), attached as Exhibit A.

STATEMENT OF FACTS
On November 12, 2021, Tree Farm LLC (“Tree Farm”) submitted to the Division both a
Notice of Intention to Commence Small Mining Operations (“Small Mine NOI”) and a Notice of
Intention to Commence Large Mining Operations (“Large Mine NOI”). On December 7, 2021,
the Division denied Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI. It explained that the “contemporaneous
submittal of these NOIs indicates Tree Farm LLC’s long-term intent is to commence operations
for a large mine,” and that in “the interest of administrative efficiency . . . [the Division] will turn
all focus and attention to the expedient review and processing of Tree Farm LLC’s Large Mine
NOI.” On December 10, 2021, Tree Farm filed a Request for Agency Action, seeking a
declaratory ruling from the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining (“Board”) regarding the completeness
of Tree Farm’s Small Mine NOI and the sufficiency of its proposed reclamation surety in order
to commence operations under its Small Mine NOI.
```

```
SUPPORT OF SALT LAKE CITY’S BRIEF
Docket No. 2022-002 Cause
No. S/035/0053

Request for Agency Action

Filing Date: March 17, 2022

I, Tamara Prue, being of lawful age, hereby swear and state as follows:
1. I am over 21 years of age.
2. I have personal knowledge of the facts stated herein.
3. I reside in Salt Lake County, Utah.
4. I am the Water Resource Manager for Salt Lake City Corporation (the “City”), and I
have been employed with the City for two years. Prior to my employment with the City, I was an
employee at the State of Utah Division of Water Rights (the “Division”) for 12 years, most recently
2

g

as an Adjudication Team Lead. I have a Horticulture degree from Utah State University.
5. Salt Lake City is the largest retail water provider in the State of Utah and has over 360,000
water customers. The City’s water assets include over 30,000 acres of property in the Wasatch
Mountain range that is designated watershed property. This includes approximately thousands of
acres of land owned by the City in Parleys Canyon. Parleys Canyon also contains the City’s
Parleys Water Treatment Plant, which processes up to 20 percent of the water used by Salt Lake
City water customers. The City maintains two reservoirs for drinking water and flood control in the
Parleys watershed.
6. The water rights in the Parleys Canyon area are administered by the Division, and the
primary guidance for relative share of the water and priority of water rights among the water users
was established by the Decree dated May 2, 1912, that adjudicated the Parleys Creek and waters by
Judge C. W. Morse. See Exhibit A. The Division commenced a modern adjudication for the
Parleys Creek Book (57-14) on October 16, 2017. The adjudication process allows all water users
to assert claims to water rights by filing a water user claim. After all water user claims are filed, the
Division identifies all “unclaimed” water rights to give water users another chance to assert claims
to use water in a drainage area. Through this process, the Division is able to evaluate the validity of
all rights in a particular drainage area.
7. The Division then issues and publishes a Proposed Determination (“PD”), which lists all
known water rights within defined boundaries of the book and identifies them as either “valid” or
“recommended to be forfeited.” The Parleys PD was published on March 1, 2022. See Exhibit B.
The PD also lists all water user claims that were 
... [truncated — full text is 5877 characters]
```

```
about issues in our state to email officials. It takes 2 minutes. I wish more people would

have a hard time hearing around the rhetoric to know what would be the best course of
action.

Michelle
```
